  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3ba0f285-875f-4369-ba6c-afe853a26b89'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer9542097303745782682">While hearts may go on after a tragedy occurs, they are never the same. Prolific bestselling author Danielle Steel revisits this familiar theme in <i>No Greater Love</i>. Twenty-year-old Edwina Winfield is forced to assume the role of head of the household, becoming both mother and father to her five younger siblings after her parents and beloved fiancé drown during the disastrou</span>
  <span id="freeText9542097303745782682" style="display:none">While hearts may go on after a tragedy occurs, they are never the same. Prolific bestselling author Danielle Steel revisits this familiar theme in <i>No Greater Love</i>. Twenty-year-old Edwina Winfield is forced to assume the role of head of the household, becoming both mother and father to her five younger siblings after her parents and beloved fiancé drown during the disastrous sinking of the <i>Titanic</i>. Determined never to marry, Edwina must also run the family newspaper until her younger brothers are old enough to step in. But next-in-line Phillip heads first to Harvard and then is tragically killed during World War I. Fun-loving George is wooed by the lights of Hollywood and exquisite sister Alexis follows in his footsteps. While tending to the youngest children, Fannie and Teddy, Edwina must assist the rest of her siblings out of their many scrapes and escapades. Along the way, she comes to terms with her loss and is finally able to put the events of the fateful night of April 15, 1912, the night the <i>Titanic</i> made its final voyage to the bottom of the sea, behind her and let love into her heart once more. <i>--Alison Trinkle</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9542097303745782682" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1628580085?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Piyangie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Piyangie" href="/user/show/48056505-piyangie">Piyangie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48056505-piyangie?shelf=my-library">my-library</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1628580085" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17224978270812325758">This is yet another beautiful book written by Danielle Steel. Being inspired by the tragedy of Titanic, Danielle Steel weaves a story about a family who survived the tragedy. Having lost both parents and finance, Edwina struggles to bring up her siblings and run the family business. Although suffering from her own grief, she nevertheless put her feelings secondary to play both the mother and father role to her younger siblings. In Edwina, Ms. Steel has created a strong, courageous woman whom rea</span>
  <span id="freeText17224978270812325758" style="display:none">This is yet another beautiful book written by Danielle Steel. Being inspired by the tragedy of Titanic, Danielle Steel weaves a story about a family who survived the tragedy. Having lost both parents and finance, Edwina struggles to bring up her siblings and run the family business. Although suffering from her own grief, she nevertheless put her feelings secondary to play both the mother and father role to her younger siblings. In Edwina, Ms. Steel has created a strong, courageous woman whom readers can take instantly to their hearts. I believe every reader of this story felt admiration towards this character, for I certainly did. Although there wasn't anything remarkable in the subsequent story line in the aftermath of the tragedy, the emotional journey of Edwina kept me engaged with the reading. The end was somehow predictable, for that is how the romances end. But in this case, I was happy that Ms. Steel didn't neglect Edwina at the end and allowed her to have a happy ending which she thoroughly deserved.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17224978270812325758" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

The first time I read this book I was in tears for most of it, although the second time round I remember the sad parts and kept myself together. It is a really great story, of romance and loss and especially of sacrifice.<br /><br />Years ago, when I was 11, I first picked up a Danielle Steel novel. It was 'Accident'.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1561789214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15724296618983200024">Once upon a time many years ago a teenaged me loved this book. That girl loved the history and romance of ocean liners and everything Edwardian. That girl also didn't know how many other well written fiction books were written about Titanic. Teenaged me grew up and some twenty (give or take a year or two) years later picked this book up again to see if the magic was there. It wasn't. I barely made it past the Titanic chapters I was so angry. The history was not only off, but she basically made i</span>
  <span id="freeText15724296618983200024" style="display:none">Once upon a time many years ago a teenaged me loved this book. That girl loved the history and romance of ocean liners and everything Edwardian. That girl also didn't know how many other well written fiction books were written about Titanic. Teenaged me grew up and some twenty (give or take a year or two) years later picked this book up again to see if the magic was there. It wasn't. I barely made it past the Titanic chapters I was so angry. The history was not only off, but she basically made it seem that real passenger Bess Allison knowingly saw her infant son into a lifeboat with a nanny while she and two year old daughter Lorraine decided to die together with her husband. Anyone with remote knowledge of the story knows that this was not true. The Allison baby was kidnapped by his nanny, they got into a boat while Mrs. Allison searched frantically for them refusing to leave without her boy. By the time she realized that he was in a boat, it was too late, and she and her toddler daughter went down with the ship, Lorraine Allison being the only first class child to die that night. That alone ticked me off rather irrationally I know and I was so angry I couldn't even finish the book again. Sadly the magic has gone for me. Was it maturity, the fact that I've found better written Titanic novels or maybe the book was never that great in the first place. Who knows. All I know is if this book angered me I'm staying well away from Zoya, which is set in Russia in 1917. That one might make my head explode with rage.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15724296618983200024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_977034198" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/977034198" />
    <a title="Marsha A. Miller" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28708524-marsha-a-miller"><img alt="Marsha A. Miller" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416770938p2/28708524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/977034198?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marsha A. Miller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marsha A. Miller" href="/user/show/28708524-marsha-a-miller">Marsha A. Miller</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6603734-no-greater-love">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer977034198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14425167074706161067"><strong>No greater book</strong><br/><br/>I have read many books by Danielle Steel but none have ever moved me the way this has. No greater love is a story about courage human endurance and most of all love. The book is based around the Winfield family and there tragic trip aboard the fated Titanic. The Winfield's have travelled to England in order to celebrate there eldest daughter's engagement to a young gentleman who is now accompanying them home to America onboard the Titanic for her maiden voyage. The tragedy unfolds</span>
  <span id="freeText14425167074706161067" style="display:none"><strong>No greater book</strong><br /><br />I have read many books by Danielle Steel but none have ever moved me the way this has. No greater love is a story about courage human endurance and most of all love. The book is based around the Winfield family and there tragic trip aboard the fated Titanic. The Winfield's have travelled to England in order to celebrate there eldest daughter's engagement to a young gentleman who is now accompanying them home to America onboard the Titanic for her maiden voyage. The tragedy unfolds as Titanic sinks and the family loose both parents and the daughter her fiance in the sinking. Upon being rescued Edwina takes on the huge task at just 19 years old of raising her 3 brothers and 2 sisters the youngest of which is just 2. Devoting her life to the children and mourning the Fiance and parents she lost her life is no longer her own. No greater love is a sad yet bittersweet look at what life was like for so many that lost loved ones the night Titanic went down. It is testimony to the strength people find out of tragedy and the way people adapt and grow despite suffering great loss. I give the book 5 stars because it is so.well written there are many books pertaining to Titanic and many love stories have been written surrounding her but very few touch the heart or speak to the soul the way this one does. This book brings tears to your eyes as you read it tears for all the lives that were lost and tears for Edwina and her family as they struggle to cope with the loss of their parents in very different ways. I strongly recommend that anyone who has an interest in Titanic reads this book or even just anyone who wants to read something that gives them hope as this book does exactly that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14425167074706161067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_181430078" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/181430078?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385299091" href="/book/show/2046193.No_Greater_Love">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4333438-mallory?shelf=another-time-and-place">another-time-and-place</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer181430078" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12271237181060001104">Because I’m a sucker for all things Titanic, I grabbed this book from the library booksale shelf several years ago. This is the first Danielle Steel novel I’ve read. I liked it a lot because of the subject material, because it falls into my favorite genre (historical fiction), but mostly because it was a really good story. Edwina’s unselfish care of her siblings after the deaths of her parents and fiancé is heartbreakingly beautiful. She never thinks of all that she is missing in life except in </span>
  <span id="freeText12271237181060001104" style="display:none">Because I’m a sucker for all things Titanic, I grabbed this book from the library booksale shelf several years ago. This is the first Danielle Steel novel I’ve read. I liked it a lot because of the subject material, because it falls into my favorite genre (historical fiction), but mostly because it was a really good story. Edwina’s unselfish care of her siblings after the deaths of her parents and fiancé is heartbreakingly beautiful. She never thinks of all that she is missing in life except in quiet, dark moments. Her whole life is devoted to her brothers and sisters and she loves them absolutely. As they begin to grow older and move away, she learns how to live and love again. <br /><br />Favorite quotes: “You’ll never be quite the same. The world will grow, and you’ll see us differently when you come home. We’ll seem very small to you, and very provincial.” – Edwina to Phillip<br /><br />“Thoughts of the Titanic kept drifting into her head… the night of the ship going down… the screech of the lifeboats being lowered… the wails of the people in the water as they drowned. How did one forget memories like that? When did it ever go away?”<br /><br />“Big challenges aren’t for everyone. Just a rare few. And the people outside those magic circles never really understand it.” – Edwina Winfield <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12271237181060001104" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1668932152" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1668932152" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31482329-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452789686p2/31482329.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1668932152?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/31482329-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/30624276-no-greater-love">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31482329-laura?shelf=books-from-mum">books-from-mum</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1668932152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11222818114202080184">It's more of a 2.5 rating.<br/><br/>Word of warning: only the beginning of the book is set on the <i>Titanic</i>, so don't pick this up if you're interested in only reading about the doomed ship. However, it's a lovely exploration of familial bonds and surviving that traumatic night.<br/><br/>Everything about it screams of the cheesy, almost airport paperback, novels your mum or great aunt secretly read but I found it increasingly difficult to put down, helped by the fact it's exceptionally easy to read [anyone looking at</span>
  <span id="freeText11222818114202080184" style="display:none">It's more of a 2.5 rating.<br /><br />Word of warning: only the beginning of the book is set on the <i>Titanic</i>, so don't pick this up if you're interested in only reading about the doomed ship. However, it's a lovely exploration of familial bonds and surviving that traumatic night.<br /><br />Everything about it screams of the cheesy, almost airport paperback, novels your mum or great aunt secretly read but I found it increasingly difficult to put down, helped by the fact it's exceptionally easy to read [anyone looking at my reading graph/progress, the lull was due to me - you can imagine it was difficult in places to read about dead parents following your own grief].<br />However, towards the end the book seemed to deflate. The issue with Alexis solved almost by <i>ex machina</i>, all of Edwina's revelations conveniently being laid out for her by Patrick, a walking plot device, and not of her own character development. <br /><br />Also, for my taste there was an unsettling amount of emphasis on Edwina needing to marry and have children. Throughout she vehemently objects, so would you if you'd had to bring up five of someone else's children, and rather than flying in the face of expectations to live life as full as any bachelor (at this point the book reaches the 1920s, a decade not exactly known for deferential women), Edwina just rolls over to the presumption that the only thing worth doing in a woman's life would be to have her own babies. Yawn!<br /><br />Still, up until the end it was enjoyable. Maybe Steel was on a tight deadline and rushed the last few chapters...</span>
  <a data-text-id="11222818114202080184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Kris - My Novelesque Life" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6275022-kris---my-novelesque-life"><img alt="Kris - My Novelesque Life" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577743166p2/6275022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1198040808?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kris - My Novelesque Life" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kris - My Novelesque Life" href="/user/show/6275022-kris---my-novelesque-life">Kris - My Novelesque Life</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385299091" href="/book/show/2046193.No_Greater_Love">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1198040808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13927266006016605181">1 STARS<br/><br/>"It was the maiden voyage of the Titanic, the greatest ship ever built, and in one fatal, unforgettable night, the sea shattered the lives and future of an extraordinary family, the Winfields.<br/><br/>Edwina Winfield, returning from her engagement trip to England with her fiance and her family, instantly loses her parents, the man she loved and her dreams. Without even time to mourn, she courageously defies convention to run her family's California newspaper and care for her five younger siblings.</span>
  <span id="freeText13927266006016605181" style="display:none">1 STARS<br /><br />"It was the maiden voyage of the Titanic, the greatest ship ever built, and in one fatal, unforgettable night, the sea shattered the lives and future of an extraordinary family, the Winfields.<br /><br />Edwina Winfield, returning from her engagement trip to England with her fiance and her family, instantly loses her parents, the man she loved and her dreams. Without even time to mourn, she courageously defies convention to run her family's California newspaper and care for her five younger siblings. Unable to forget her fiance Charles, she is determined never to marry, to keep her family together, and to fight to survive as a woman alone. But Phillip, her beloved oldest brother, sets out for Harvard and tragically betrays her trust. Madcap brother George turns to the excitement of Hollywood during its magical days, not to the Winfield publishing empire. And lovely Alexis, who narrowly escaped death when the Titanic went down, grows into a troubled runaway whom even Edwina's love may not be able to save. The two youngest, Fannie and Teddy, remain with Edwina at home." (From Amazon)<br /><br />Originally when I read Danielle Steel novels I would have rated them 3-4 STARS, but now I would classify them as 1-2 STARS. These are great for those who like mild sex, unrealistic dramatic romances and grand plots. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13927266006016605181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer179207970" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1059207267868732323">Between 2.5 and 3 stars. I would've loved this book in middle school! I liked the Titanic aspect and it surprised me that this was written before the movie came out. The elements of the boarding, first class life, and the sinking were exactly like the movie. I didn't like the flow of them book and it would definitely have been edited way down had it been written in current time. There were no real paragraphs or start/stop to people's thoughts. The titanic part is over relatively quickly and then</span>
  <span id="freeText1059207267868732323" style="display:none">Between 2.5 and 3 stars. I would've loved this book in middle school! I liked the Titanic aspect and it surprised me that this was written before the movie came out. The elements of the boarding, first class life, and the sinking were exactly like the movie. I didn't like the flow of them book and it would definitely have been edited way down had it been written in current time. There were no real paragraphs or start/stop to people's thoughts. The titanic part is over relatively quickly and then it followed the survivors through their lives in show business and learning to love again. Overall fun but the writing was really painful to read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1059207267868732323" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_96790531" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96790531" />
    <a title="Kellylynn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3204545-kellylynn"><img alt="Kellylynn" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96790531?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kellylynn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kellylynn" href="/user/show/3204545-kellylynn">Kellylynn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96790531" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10122257398606090178">A story about the 'perfect' family and what happens to them after the sinking of the Titanic. Rather predictable and very simplistically written, which makes for a very fast and easy read. You feel bad for the family and all that the children endure during the sinking. But as their lives move on the story just gets a little grating on how the eldest daughter struggles to keep the family together. It is a nice story of overcoming fears and prejudices.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_836424593" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/836424593" />
    <a title="Jill Friesz rhamy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28089029-jill-friesz-rhamy"><img alt="Jill Friesz rhamy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390794820p2/28089029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/836424593?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jill Friesz rhamy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jill Friesz rhamy" href="/user/show/28089029-jill-friesz-rhamy">Jill Friesz rhamy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer836424593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13819676417368707001">I am not a huge Danielle Steel fan, but I have to list this as one of my favorite books of all time. It was the first book I read for just pure pleasure. I read this book the summer before I was a sophomore in college and it still remains one of my favorites. I loved the richness of the characters and the passage of time in the book through the Titanic, World War 1, etc. </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1877089205" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1877089205" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47645617-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484755375p2/47645617.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1877089205?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/47645617-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1877089205&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1877089205" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer489640517202305248">I had never read a Danielle Steel book before this one, and after years of seeing them lined up on the shelves at the book store in the vicinity of the likes of Julia Quinn and Nora Roberts, I seem to have gotten the preconceived notion that Steel's genre is romance. Despite what the title and setting would perhaps have you believe, "No Greater Love" was egregiously soft in the romance department. Out of four-hundred or so pages, our protagonist spends roughly less than fifty of them engaged in </span>
  <span id="freeText489640517202305248" style="display:none">I had never read a Danielle Steel book before this one, and after years of seeing them lined up on the shelves at the book store in the vicinity of the likes of Julia Quinn and Nora Roberts, I seem to have gotten the preconceived notion that Steel's genre is romance. Despite what the title and setting would perhaps have you believe, "No Greater Love" was egregiously soft in the romance department. Out of four-hundred or so pages, our protagonist spends roughly less than fifty of them engaged in conversation with anyone outside of her own family, let alone experiencing romantic interaction. <br /><br />If you are expecting the Titanic to feature heavily in the narrative, best be prepared for the fact that it sinks thirty pages in, leaving us to watch as protagonist Edwina is left to raise her five now-orphaned younger siblings. When I mentioned this to a close friend who is particularly well-versed in the romance genre, she laughed and said - having never read this book but familiar with Ms. Steel's modus operandi: "prepare to cover the next 3-5 decades of this woman's life." And she was correct -- Steel takes us from the sinking of the Titanic, through to the outbreak of WWI, and the rise of Hollywood and swinger culture in the 1920's. Over which time, Murphy's Law presides: if it can go badly for this family, it will. Right up to a climax wherein Edwina takes a two-week vacation from searching for her kidnapped younger sister to have a dalliance with a married man. ("I'm sure she'll be fine, pour some more champagne, Patrick!" Isn't something that was said, but could have been.) Leading to an ending where Edwina settles on and marries her brother's new father-in-law because, well he happens to stand still long enough to get married to on the last page, I suppose. <br /><br />The twists and turns of the plot are melodramatic at best, but the real weakness is Steel's uninspiring use of the otherwise lush historical settings the book features. The dialogue and characters could easily have been plucked from a more contemporary time period and dropped in front of the painted backdrop of San Francisco in the 1910's. Simple, modern language makes for an easy read, but there isn't much to gain from this book outside of a few hours of modest entertainment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="489640517202305248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3111222843" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13895766998540504847">April 1912,London.<br/>Kate and Bert with their six children stay with her sister Liz .The family is to sail back to the States on Titanic. <br/>Edwina, the eldest, is 20, engaged to Charles, who is sailing with them .Other children range from 16 to 2 yo.<br/>When she ship sinks, Kate stays behind with Bert. She is in a different boat.Edwina sees Titanic go down and realizes she h</span>
  <span id="freeText13895766998540504847" style="display:none">April 1912,London.<br />Kate and Bert with their six children stay with her sister Liz .The family is to sail back to the States on Titanic. <br />Edwina, the eldest, is 20, engaged to Charles, who is sailing with them .Other children range from 16 to 2 yo.<br />When she ship sinks, Kate stays behind with Bert. Charles stays behind, too.One of the girls, Alexis (it's her 6th birthday) stays in the cabin and is rescued by one of the sailors. She is in a different boat.Edwina sees Titanic go down and realizes she has lost both her parents and her fiance.She is now head of the family.There is Philip (16), a serious young man expected to continue the family newspaper business. George (12 ) is a clown dreaming of going to Hollywood . Alexis (6 ) is shy, traumatized by being separated from her siblings and parents. Fanny is 4 and the baby, Teddy, is only 2. <br />The siblings return home and try to survive.<br />Life goes on. In 1914 Philip starts Harvard, only to enlist in 1917. He is sent to France and falls in one of the battles.<br />When Liz and her titled husband die, the siblings inherit some money.<br />George moves to Hollywood,becoming partner of Sam Horowitz and producing films. He marries Sam's daughter Helen. Now he is the responsible male of the family. <br />Alexis is a beauty and is searching for a father figure .In 1923, at 17 ,she has her first role .She is seduced by Malcolm Stone (50 ), who pretends to marry Alexis. <br />Fanny, at 15, is a homebody,while Teddy at 13 is a typical teenager.<br />Edwina has twice turned down her father's friend ,Ben Jones , a widower. She stays single, devoting herself to her siblings. <br />When Alexis elopes with Malcolm to England (she is petrified on the ship and is sedated ), Edwina rushes after her. Edwina meets Patrick, who is...Charles's cousin ! Patrick ,a Catholic, is married ,although doesn't live with his wife. Edwina falls in love with him ,realizing there is no future for them.<br />So, at 32, Edwina accepts... Sam Horowitz , who is in his 50s.<br />Interesting story, many famous names are mentioned- both on Titanic and in Hollywood. <br />Would love an epilogue..</span>
  <a data-text-id="13895766998540504847" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2931260244&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2931260244" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6861214311231738018">This was a difficult book to rate. I liked it, although the entirety of the book was rather depressing. Of course, that can't be avoided since Edwina and her family were aboard the Titanic. So, it was realistically depressing. I enjoyed learning about life on the Titanic, although as another reviewer pointed out, it wasn't completely historically accurate. I sympathized with Edwina, who was a very strong protagonist, and admire her for her perseverance and selflessness. She remained a rock for h</span>
  <span id="freeText6861214311231738018" style="display:none">This was a difficult book to rate. I liked it, although the entirety of the book was rather depressing. Of course, that can't be avoided since Edwina and her family were aboard the Titanic. So, it was realistically depressing. I enjoyed learning about life on the Titanic, although as another reviewer pointed out, it wasn't completely historically accurate. I sympathized with Edwina, who was a very strong protagonist, and admire her for her perseverance and selflessness. She remained a rock for her siblings and gave her all to them, even when further tragedy occurred. <br /><br />Now, the love story. I felt like the love story (which was very minimal and only touched on in the last quarter of the book) was a let down. She (finally!) meets Patrick, who she believes is the love of her life, and then must leave him. She then gets a proposal from another man whom she had never considered romantically before and decides immediately that she actually loves him. The end. This literally occurs in the last scene, and is only one short conversation. I didn't like this, nor did I find it very believable. It's a very distorted case of insta-love snatched from the present and pasted in the past. It felt more like Edwina was settling for an arranged marriage than finding her partner in life. <br /><br />Overall, the romance was awful, but the main story-line of a young girl surviving the Titanic and caring for her siblings was inspiring, enticing and heart-wrenching. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6861214311231738018" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3439023365" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3439023365" />
    <a title="Kat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2495415-kat"><img alt="Kat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346220670p2/2495415.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3439023365?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat" href="/user/show/2495415-kat">Kat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3439023365&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3439023365" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer931582369157942211">This is my second Danielle Steele book and I was a bit torn by it. I too am taken in by tales of the Titanic. However, Being a mother I can not even begin to imagine leaving my 5 children orphaned and fending for themselves. Her children were so young and still dependent on their mother. She didn’t want to leave her husband?? So she chose to die with him rather than face life without him. She then burdens her 20 year old daughter to abandon her fiancé and now mother and father her 5 siblings and</span>
  <span id="freeText931582369157942211" style="display:none">This is my second Danielle Steele book and I was a bit torn by it. I too am taken in by tales of the Titanic. However, Being a mother I can not even begin to imagine leaving my 5 children orphaned and fending for themselves. Her children were so young and still dependent on their mother. She didn’t want to leave her husband?? So she chose to die with him rather than face life without him. She then burdens her 20 year old daughter to abandon her fiancé and now mother and father her 5 siblings and take care of the family business. Unbelievably selfish! Edwina the 20 year old is a well written character and she saves the book. Strong, devoted and loving she is an amazing woman and, as we are often reminded frequently, a striking beauty. Her struggles raising the children seem real enough. Her handling of them is courageous and kind. I enjoyed the book despite the plot and it’s later attempts to whitewash the mother’s choice by saying maybe she thought she could have gotten on a later lifeboat. It was a bit repetitive at times especially describing the children’s characters. We are reminded again and again of George’s boyish qualities, Alexis’s striking blond beauty and Phillip’s serious nature. Like I said I still liked it enough but I can only give it 3 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="931582369157942211" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eileen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eileen" href="/user/show/3915172-eileen">Eileen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3915172-eileen?shelf=bookclub-selections">bookclub-selections</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3915172-eileen?shelf=across-the-usa">across-the-usa</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2023967848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8522553626448467782"><b> California</b> <br/> The writing style was too repetitive for me - when Edwina thought about Charles it was almost a word for word repeat of the last time she thought about him, <i> she had lost him and she wanted no one else only Charles </i>. Her thoughts about her parents, fit with her anger towards them but were also very repetitive. Tears streamed down cheeks more often than I cared to count and someone was always telling Edwina she was missing out on life and needed to get married. <br/><br/> Edwina is the center </span>
  <span id="freeText8522553626448467782" style="display:none"><b> California</b> <br /> The writing style was too repetitive for me - when Edwina thought about Charles it was almost a word for word repeat of the last time she thought about him, <i> she had lost him and she wanted no one else only Charles </i>. Her thoughts about her parents, fit with her anger towards them but were also very repetitive. Tears streamed down cheeks more often than I cared to count and someone was always telling Edwina she was missing out on life and needed to get married. <br /><br /> Edwina is the center of the story but the action happens with her brothers Philip and George and her sister Alexis until the very last part of the book when she is forced into action to save Alexis once again and things in her life finally move ahead. This really works nicely with the whole idea that Edwina has put her life on hold to raise her siblings. Although I have to agree with other reviewers that Patrick was a convenient plot device used to verbally set her free and the end felt rushed. <br /> <b>2.5 stars</b></span>

<div id="review_2085193511" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2085193511?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PJ" href="/user/show/4976081-pj">PJ</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4976081-pj?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4976081-pj?shelf=overcoming-adversity">overcoming-adversity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4976081-pj?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2085193511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12824844974620860030">I felt like the author was teasing me with plot ideas. The book starts with tragedy (The Titanic) and then the whole way through I felt like other bad things were going to happen to the family. A couple of bad things did happen but not as many as it seemed could happen by the writing. Then, near the end of the book, the main character does something so OUT of character for her, that when the book quickly finished with what I thought would happen all along, I was frustrated and in disbelief. I do</span>
  <span id="freeText12824844974620860030" style="display:none">I felt like the author was teasing me with plot ideas. The book starts with tragedy (The Titanic) and then the whole way through I felt like other bad things were going to happen to the family. A couple of bad things did happen but not as many as it seemed could happen by the writing. Then, near the end of the book, the main character does something so OUT of character for her, that when the book quickly finished with what I thought would happen all along, I was frustrated and in disbelief. I don't think that main character could have changed so quickly and done something so out of the norm for her and then so quickly gotten back into character. It just didn't make sense. I went along with it and enjoyed it till the last few chapters. Just left a bad taste in my mouth because it was not believable for me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12824844974620860030" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6aHbwFp4AB4/XP5Hf4cKADGlaE905cpBwSnVqHPCxc1KfB1KlRclSiQynxoeXnqoUXVGYp7g+enFfYfxz94NmA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0m0HbdlgNBzpFFDQJhsFiR+D1jbXurgAE4v7O0pmHdhxsMHnFg8RSPJ6MY1HwnUhf1P4Gz2/i6gX36li9nrVjQ==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/14255.Danielle_Steel">About Danielle Steel</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17855180197121782260">Danielle Fernandes Dominique Schuelein-Steel was born on 14 August 1947 in New York City to a German-Jewish father and a Portuguese Catholic mother, and she spent much of her childhood in France. From an education in New York and Europe to a professional background in public relations and advertising, and teaching, Ms. Steel moved on quickly to her literary career and has been hard at work writing</span>
  <span id="freeText17855180197121782260" style="display:none">Danielle Fernandes Dominique Schuelein-Steel was born on 14 August 1947 in New York City to a German-Jewish father and a Portuguese Catholic mother, and she spent much of her childhood in France. From an education in New York and Europe to a professional background in public relations and advertising, and teaching, Ms. Steel moved on quickly to her literary career and has been hard at work writing ever since. She wrote her first book at nineteen, but she didn't publish her first novel until 1973.<br /><br />Often, she works on five books at a time — researching one storyline, writing another, and editing the third. Still, she often spends two to three years researching and developing a single project. In the heat of a first draft, it is not uncommon for her to spend eighteen to twenty hours a day glued to her 1946 Olympia manual typewriter. <br /><br />Since 1979, more than twenty of Ms. Steel's novels have been adapted for television, each earning high ratings and critical acclaim, including two Golden Globe nominations for JEWELS, a four-hour mini-series that starred Anthony Andrews.<br /><br />Since 1981, Ms. Steel has been a permanent fixture on the New York Times hardcover and paperback bestseller lists. In 1989, she was listed in the Guinness Book of World Records for having at least one of her books on the Times bestseller list for 381 consecutive weeks. But Guinness was premature. The fact is that one or more of Ms. Steel's novels have been on the New York Times bestseller list for over 390 consecutive weeks. <br /><br />In addition, Ms. Steel is the author of the "Max and Martha" series of books for young readers. They are ten illustrated storybooks written to comfort the young as they face problems, such as a new stepfather, new baby, new school, loss of a grandparent, and other crucial dilemmas in a child's life. She has also written the "Freddie" books, four of them, about real-life situations in children's lives, like a visit to the doctor and the first night away from home.<br /><br />Ms. Steel has also written nonfiction, HIS BRIGHT LIGHT, about the life and death of her son Nicholas Traina, released by Delacorte Press in September 1998 and immediately jumped to the New York Times Non-Fiction bestseller list and "Having a Baby." She has also written a book of poetry entitled LOVE: POEMS BY DANIELLE STEEL. <br /><br />In 2002, Ms. Steel was decorated by the French government as an "Officier" of the distinguished Order of Arts and Letters, for her lifetime contribution to world culture. She was awarded the second highest rank of the Order. <br /><br />Ms. Steel also has a passionate interest in emerging contemporary artists. She has had an art gallery for several years, and and continues to sponsor and organize free lance art shows and events to show the work of emerging and mid-career artists. She has a degree in design herself. In addition to her writing, Ms. Steel has varied philanthropic interests. She founded and runs two foundations, one named in honor of her late son, The Nick Traina Foundation, which funds organizations involved in mental illness and child abuse. The second was established to assist the homeless. She has won numerous awards for her personal work with mentally ill adolescents and children. Ms. Steel maintains a passionate interest in the welfare and well-being of children, particularly those in jeopardy. Afther, five marriages, she has raised nine children of her own. And they continue to keep her busy, as she juggles writing and family. Her family is her first priority, despite her many interests. <br /><br />Family, children, and young people are the central focus of her life, and her passion, which frequently shows in her writing. She deals with the themes that touch on the most pressing issues of real life, which makes her books universal, and touch so many people. She is fascinated by the pressing life situations that affect us all, how people handle them and are often transformed as a result. And her novels have explored subjects such as kidnappin</span>
  <a data-text-id="17855180197121782260" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
